ගරු මහාචාර්ය ඩබ්ලිව්. ඒ. විශ්වා වර්ණපාල මහතා (மாண்ᾗமிகு (ேபராசிாியர்) டபிள்ᾝ. ஏ. விஸ்வா வர்ணபால) (The Hon. (Prof.) W.A. Wiswa Warnapala) Mr. Speaker, apart from creating the University Grants Commission and the USAB, and decentralizing the single university which was a unitary university, the 1978 piece of legislation referred to the powers of the Minister of Higher Education. Under this Act which was enacted in 1978, the Minister enjoys certain powers, and he can give written instructions to the UGC on specified matters pertaining to the establishment and administration of the universities. This Act has been amended on a number of occasions, and the last amendment was in 1995. I, in my capacity as the Deputy Minister of Higher Education, was associated with the last amendment with which we reduced the period of office of the Vice-Chancellor to two terms which means, -

කථානායකතුමා (சபாநாயகர் அவர்கள்) (Mr. Speaker) කරුණාකර ෙදපැත්ෙත්ම අය නිශ්ශබ්ද වන්න. ගරු ඇමතිතුමාට බාධා කරන්න එපා.

ගරු මහාචාර්ය ඩබ්ලිව්. ඒ. විශ්වා වර්ණපාල මහතා (மாண்ᾗமிகு (ேபராசிாியர்) டபிள்ᾝ. ஏ. விஸ்வா வர்ணபால) (The Hon. (Prof.) W.A. Wiswa Warnapala)

- Mr. Speaker, that a Vice-Chancellor can remain in office for a period of six years. This Act, which was enacted in 1978, was in operation for more than 27 years and various defects were identified and they needed to be corrected in order to achieve both administrative efficiency and proper academic control within our universities.

2009 සැප්තැම්බර් 08 1865 1866

Yet another defect was that certain provisions of the 1978 Act did not fall in line with certain changes in public policy in other spheres of governmental activity in this country. Therefore, Mr. Speaker, the University Grants Commission, as the apex body in the field of higher education in this country, examined those special provisions in the Act which needed revision and recommended a few amendments which are to be debated today in this House. Section 48 of the principal enactment - I refer to the principal piece of legislation which was introduced in 1978 - which dealt with the composition of the Faculty is to be amended with these new amendments in order to include Senior Professors and Lecturers (Probationary) as members of the Faculties of the University. In the past, the Assistant Lecturers enjoyed this opportunity and now it has been extended to Lecturers (Probationary). The purpose is to expand the Faculty. The base of the Faculty has been expanded by this amendment and the Faculty in future will include the following: (1) all permanent Senior Professors, Professors, Associate Professors, Senior Lecturers and Lecturers of the Departments of Study; (2) two members elected by the Lecturers (Probationary) of the Faculty; and (3) two members of the permanent staff of instructors. Mr. Speaker, there are three major components in any modern university, for that matter - Administration, Faculty and Students. A university, as you know very well, Mr. Speaker, is a community of scholars dedicated to the preservation, advancement and transmission of knowledge. It is a knowledge-creating body. In any university, the branches of study are broadly divided into Faculties and they are subdivided into Departments. It is on the basis of this division that both teaching and research are organized and conducted in a university. Therefore, the Faculty is subordinate to the Senate, which as you know, is the highest academic body in a given university. It is the Senate which takes all academic decisions and the argument has been made that the powers of the Senate need to be expanded to include powers pertaining to discipline as well. It needs to be done. Section 71 of the principal enactment is to be amended to provide for the Commission to determine the salary points of employees who are not teachers and they are to be appointed on the basis of the recommendation of the Higher Educational Institutions. කථානායකතුමා (சபாநாயகர் அவர்கள்) (Mr. Speaker) කරුණාකර නිශ්ශබ්ද වන්න. ෙම් අවස්ථාෙව්දී ගරු නිෙයෝජɕ කථානායකතුමා මූලාසනය ගන්නවා ඇත.

අනතුරුව කථානායකතුමා මූලාසනෙයන් ඉවත් වුෙයන්, නිෙයෝජɕ කථානායකතුමා [ගරු පියංකර ජයරත්න මහතා] මූලාසනාරූඪ විය.

அதன்பிறகு, சபாநாயகர் அவர்கள் அக்கிராசனத்தினின்ᾠ அகலேவ, பிரதிச் சபாநாயகர் அவர்கள் [மாண்ᾗமிகு பியங்கர ஜயரத்ன] தைலைம வகித்தார்கள்.

Whereupon MR. SPEAKER left the Chair, and MR. DEPUTY SPEAKER [THE HON. PIYANKARA JAYARATNE] took the Chair.

ගරු මහාචාර්ය ඩබ්ලිව්. ඒ. විශ්වා වර්ණපාල මහතා (மாண்ᾗமிகு (ேபராசிாியர்) டபிள்ᾝ. ஏ. விஸ்வா வர்ணபால) (The Hon. (Prof.) W.A. Wiswa Warnapala) Mr. Deputy Speaker, I am referring to a particular provision in the legislation, which is to be amended. This provision, in my view, has expanded the autonomy and independence of the Higher Educational Institutions which come under the purview of the University Grants Commission. In other words, some of these amendments, in my view, expand the autonomy and independence of our universities in this country. That is a good thing because we need to preserve the independence and autonomy of our universities.

The next amendment, which proposes to amend subsection (1) of Section 72 of the 1978 Act, relates to the need to serve a probationary period of one year and this applies to teachers who have been previously confirmed in a post in another Higher Educational Institution.

The next amendment is a vital concession extended to all the non-academic employees of this country. According to Section 75 of the original piece of legislation, an employee was expected to retire at the age of 55. A person was able to obtain extensions up to the 60th year and that was subject to a number of conditions. The amendment which is before this House today proposes to change the optional age of retirement to 57, a vital concession to the non-academic employees in the university. They need to be happy about it, which means that a person can now continue to remain in service until he completes his 57th year. This, in my view, is a major concession extended to all the non-academic employees of the universities and all trade unions have applauded this decision.

In the last amendment, the definition of the word “Teacher” has been changed to include the following: Senior Professors, Professors, Senior Lecturers, Lecturers and Lecturers (Probationary). Mr. Deputy Speaker, these are the things which I need to mention in respect of the amendments.

Now, I would like to seize the opportunity to provide the House with certain basic facts relating to university education in Sri Lanka. Our system has been commended by the World Bank. I have here with me a book published by the World Bank titled "The Towers of Learning", which they produced a couple of days back. I am sure my good, learned Colleague, the Hon. (Dr.) Sarath Amunugama, would have seen this. This is what its Executive Summary states. I will quote the second paragraph:

“The higher education sector can and must lead Sri Lanka successfully over the crests of these two waves of golden opportunity. Higher education institutions should drive and accelerate the country’s ascent to middle-income (MIC) status. Also, the higher education system should inspire the country’s values, ethics and social institutions so that Sri Lanka becomes celebrated as an enlightened and peaceful multi-ethnic, multi-religious and multi-cultural society.

පාර්ලිෙම්න්තුව 1867 1868

This is what they say in respect of our higher education. They have commended our proposals. Our higher education system has been commended by the World Bank, which has agreed to support us till 2015. The Deputy Minister of Finance and Planning, my good Friend, the Hon. (Dr.) Sarath Amunugama, will be happy to hear that the World Bank is willing to support the higher education system till 2015, within which period we propose to bring about a comprehensive change in the system with a view to converting our universities into global centres of excellence; we want to convert our universities into global centres of learning. This can be achieved only with the co-operation of the undergraduate community. Let me begin with the progress we made in respect of the buildings and the rest of it. With regard to admissions, we have made a couple of achievements. In 2006, we admitted 17,248 students. In 2007, it was increased to 20,069 and in 2008, we admitted 20,846 students. Every year we made an increase. This is a major improvement and we propose to increase the intake to 25,000 in the next two years. In terms of global standards, Mr. Deputy Speaker, the public investment in higher education is comparatively low. I accept that. This was due to various constraints in the Sri Lankan economy in the last 30 years. Public investment in higher education in terms of GDP is still low. In other words, it is 0.5 per cent of GDP and only 18 per cent of the public Budget is allocated to higher education. Despite the nature of investment, which, in my view, - ගරු රවි කරුණානායක මහතා (மாண்ᾗமிகு ரவி கᾞணாநாயக்க) (The Hon. Ravi Karunanayake) Hon. Minister - ගරු මහාචාර්ය ඩබ්ලිව්. ඒ. විශ්වා වර්ණපාල මහතා (மாண்ᾗமிகு (ேபராசிாியர்) டபிள்ᾝ. ஏ. விஸ்வா வர்ணபால) (The Hon. (Prof.) W.A. Wiswa Warnapala)

Please do not interrupt me. I am not giving way. I have no time. Please do not interrupt. I am not giving way. You have been used to these kinds of interruptions. Some of them are useful; some of them are absolutely useless.

Despite the nature of investment, we have achieved a commendable progress within the system. We are now in the process of modernizing the curricular of the universities. Mr. Deputy Speaker, the curricular is fairly old. It needs to be modernized in the interest of better performance of our graduates from the universities. Now we want to break away from the traditional disciplines which dominated the university since 1942 or for that matter, dominated the system in the last 60 years. The traditional disciplines served a purpose at that particular point of time, but now we need to make changes. We need market-oriented courses with which we can produce

an employable graduate. That is our aim. We want to produce graduates who can find employment in the competitive labour market.

Now the system has 86 courses for which students are annually selected. In 2006, we introduced a couple of new courses. In 2007, ten more new courses were introduced and in 2008 another six courses were added. We have done the changes in keeping with the global changes in the field of higher education. One problem within the system was the failure to work according to the University Calendar. Now we have fixed common dates or common days for the commencement and the conclusion of the undergraduate academic programmes of the undergraduate academic year, and this is to be implemented in the academic year 2008 and 2009. In the area of academic development, two new Faculties were established both at Peradeniya and Rajarata. Thirty six new Departments of Study have been established in the last three years, and the aim was to modernize the course structure in the universities so that you can produce people who can obtain employment in a competitive employment market. It is only on the basis of such changes, Mr. Deputy Speaker, that we can produce employable graduates.

Yet another thing which we have undertaken is the re-examination of the external degree programmes of the universities. Universities expanded the external degree programmes in order to provide more access to higher educational opportunities. The external degree programmes were introduced in order to give more opportunities to students to obtain a higher educational qualification. In Sri Lanka, external degree programmes are conducted or offered by 11 universities and cater to our student clientele - you will be surprised to hear - of nearly 175,000. Certain universities register more than 75,000 or sometimes more than 50,000 students. The quality of external graduates has declined, and therefore measures are being taken or measures are immediately necessary to improve the quality of the external graduates. In future, students will be admitted only on the basis of the Z-score. A minimum level will be established for this purpose. Otherwise, every Tom, Dick and Harry can get into the course, go into one of the poorly-administered tuition classes, collect a couple of notes, sit the exam and pass it. We do not want to produce such graduates in the future. We want to produce a quality graduate even through the external degree programmes.

In Sri Lanka, the emphasis has been on undergraduate education. Mr. Deputy Speaker, all of us know that since 1921 when the University College was established during colonial time and since 1942 when an Independent Autonomous University was established under the colonial regime again, our emphasis was primarily on undergraduate education. It was this reason which led to the neglect of the postgraduate sector. A postgraduate intellectual culture is fundamentally necessary if one wants to make an impact on the learning environment of

[ගරු මහාචාර්ය ඩබ්ලිව්. ඒ. විශ්වා වර්ණපාල මහතා]

2009 සැප්තැම්බර් 08 1869 1870

3 - PL 004365 - (2009/09)

the undergraduate. A postgraduate intellectual culture needs to be promoted and restored in order to change the learning environment in our universities. Most of our undergraduates do not want to learn; they want to go pasting posters all over the country or carrying a “kete” in order to collect money. No university will be allowed to conduct postgraduate courses without the approval of the University Grants Commission because that too needs to be streamlined; that needs to be properly controlled, so that we can produce good postgraduates with qualifications which are acceptable to the outside world. A Faculty of Graduate Studies needs to be created for the purpose of promoting postgraduate education. Another important matter on which the Ministry has taken a decision was the need for a Common National Qualification Framework. I am sure my learned Friend, the Hon. (Dr.) Amunugama will be happy to hear this. This country, Hon. Kiriella, needs a Common National Qualification Framework because there are bogus providers. Yesterday, I read in a newspaper that there is a small factory in Matale which is producing degree certificates. Therefore, there are bogus producers. This kind of thing needs to be stopped. Such a National Qualification Framework is necessary to discourage bogus providers in this country. In any case, the country at this given point of time needs a National Qualification Framework in order to maintain standards, consistency and comparability of university level qualification. නිෙයෝජɕ කථානායකතුමා (பிரதிச் சபாநாயகர் அவர்கள்) (The Deputy Speaker) Hon. Minister, your time is over. ගරු මහාචාර්ය ඩබ්ලිව්. ඒ. විශ්වා වර්ණපාල මහතා (மாண்ᾗமிகு (ேபராசிாியர்) டபிள்ᾝ. ஏ. விஸ்வா வர்ணபால) (The Hon. (Prof.) W.A. Wiswa Warnapala)

I have been given 30 minutes and the Hon. Chief Government Whip told me that I might be able to get ten more minutes from the other speakers. Is it okay?

නිෙයෝජɕ කථානායකතුමා (பிரதிச் சபாநாயகர் அவர்கள்) (The Deputy Speaker)

You have been allocated only 22 minutes and you have already finished that.

ගරු මහාචාර්ය ඩබ්ලිව්. ඒ. විශ්වා වර්ණපාල මහතා (மாண்ᾗமிகு (ேபராசிாியர்) டபிள்ᾝ. ஏ. விஸ்வா வர்ணபால) (The Hon. (Prof.) W.A. Wiswa Warnapala)

Since the emergence of the Mahinda Rajapaksa regime, several measures have been taken to improve the infrastructure facilities of the universities. Impressive achievements have been recorded in respect of infrastructure development. Thirty five construction projects have been completed in order to provide facilities for teaching, learning and accommodation. There are 49

on-going projects the cost of which is around Rs. 10,429 million. In addition, there are 31 projects for which approval has been given by the Department of National Planning. There are another 18 projects, the estimated cost of which is Rs. 4,020 million. It has been approved by the Cabinet.

Measures have been taken to curb ragging. This is a thing on which, Mr. Deputy Speaker, I need to speak. You need to give me a little bit of time because I need to speak a couple of words on ragging. නවක වදය ගැනත් මා ෙම් පාර්ලිෙම්න්තුෙව් කියන්න ඕනෑ.

Measures have been taken to curb ragging in the universities. The incidents of ragging need to be dealt with under the Prevention of Ragging Act. It is the piece of legislation with which you were also associated, with which all of us were associated when it was passed in 1997. It is my concerned view that strict measures are necessary to prevent ragging in the universities. Ragging and other forms of violence destabilize the universities, and the learning environment is disrupted. I need to mention this. I read an article in the “The Economist” of London referring to ragging in India. In India, strong measures have been taken to curb ragging and every university’s gate - ඇතුළු වන ෙදොරටුව ළඟ - has the poster which says, “An Act of Ragging May Land You in Jail”. ඉන්දියාෙව් හැම විශ්වවිදɕාලයකම ෙදොරටුෙව් අලවලා තිෙබනවා, “නවක වදය දුන්ෙනොත් හිර ෙගදරට යන්න ෙවයි” කියලා. අපටත් දැන් ඒක අලවන්න සිද්ධ ෙවයි කියලා මා විශ්වාස කරනවා.

The Indian Government which sees ragging as a criminal offence - the Indian Supreme Court treats ragging as a criminal offence - is determined to deal with those elements which indulge in violent ragging. Recently, an 18-year old medical student was beaten to death in Northern State of Himalchal Pradesh during a ragging ceremony. A voluntary organization has been formed in India to curb ragging. This is the name of the organization, “Coalition to Uproot Ragging from Education”. ඒ කියන්ෙන් නවක වදය වැළැක්වීම සඳහා ස්ෙව්ච්ඡා සංවිධානයක් මුළුමහත් ඉන්දියාෙව්ම නිර්මාණය කර තිෙබනවා. හැබැයි මීට පස්ෙසේ ලංකාෙව් විශ්වවිදɕාලයක නවක වදය දීලා ඔප්පු වුෙණෝතින් ඒ ශිෂɕයාෙග් ශිෂɕභාවය අෙහෝසි කරන්නය කියලා මා විශ්වවිදɕාලපතිපාදන ෙකොමිෂන් සභාවට උපෙදස් දීලා තිෙබනවා. ඉතාමත්ම නරක විධියට නවක වදය ෙදනවා නම් ඔහු උසස් අධɕාපනයට සුදුසු නැහැ; ඔහු විශ්වවිදɕාල අධɕාපනයට සුදුසු නැහැ. මට ඊෙය්- ෙපෙර්දා ෙමොරටුව විශ්වවිදɕාලෙයන් එක සිද්ධියක් ආරංචි වුණා. ගැහැනු ළමෙයක් ආහාර ගත්තාට පස්ෙසේ ඒ ළමයාට පැය හතරක් අත ෙහෝදන්න දීලා නැහැ. ඒ වාෙග් ශිෂɕ පරම්පරාවකින් ෙම් රට හදන්න පුළුවන්ද? ඒ වාෙග් ශිෂɕ පරම්පරාවකින් ෙම් රට ෙව්ගවත් සංවර්ධිත ෙලෝකයකට ෙගන යන්න පුළුවන්ද? තවත් සිද්ධියක් මට වාර්තා වුණා. Toilet එකට මළ පහ කළායින් පස්ෙසේ නවක ශිෂɕයකු ෙගනැල්ලා commode එකට මුහුණ තියන්නය කියලා flush කර තිෙබනවා. ඊළඟට පැදුරක් විතර කුණු හරුප වැලක් ලියලා, අවුරුදු 17ක් විතර වයසැති ගැහැනු ළමෙයකුට දීලා ඒක හඬ නඟා කියවන්නය කියලා තිෙබනවා. ඒක පිටි පස්ෙසේ ෙද්ශපාලනයකුත් තිෙබනවා. ඒක ගැනත් අපට යථා කාලෙය්දී කියන්න ෙවයි. ඉතින් ෙම් විධියටයි අද ෙම් rag එක පාවිච්චි කරන්ෙන්. Therefore, I do not want to speak anymore on

පාර්ලිෙම්න්තුව 1871 1872

this. Even in Tamil Nadu, they passed a piece of legislation to curb ragging. In February, 2009 - I am sure my good Friend, the Hon. Lakshman Kiriella, will be happy to hear this - the Supreme Court of India declared ragging as "a human rights abuse in essence"; that in essence, ragging could be treated as a human rights abuse and ordered measures to stamp it out. Closed-circuit television cameras have been installed both at the University of Delhi and the Jawaharlal Nehru University to prevent ragging. Both students and parents should co-operate with us to get rid of this menace. නිෙයෝජɕ කථානායකතුමා (பிரதிச் சபாநாயகர் அவர்கள்) (The Deputy Speaker) ගරු ඇමතිතුමා, ඔබතුමාෙග් කථාව අවසන් කරන්න. ගරු මහාචාර්ය ඩබ්ලිව්. ඒ. විශ්වා වර්ණපාල මහතා (மாண்ᾗமிகு (ேபராசிாியர்) டபிள்ᾝ. ஏ. விஸ்வா வர்ணபால) (The Hon. (Prof.) W.A. Wiswa Warnapala) ගරු නිෙයෝජɕ කථානායකතුමනි, මට තව විනාඩි පහක් ෙදන්න.

නිෙයෝජɕ කථානායකතුමා (பிரதிச் சபாநாயகர் அவர்கள்) (The Deputy Speaker) ගරු ඇමතිතුමා, ඒක කරන්න අමාරුයි. උෙද් පමාදෙය් පතිඵලය තමයි.

ගරු මහාචාර්ය ඩබ්ලිව්. ඒ. විශ්වා වර්ණපාල මහතා (மாண்ᾗமிகு (ேபராசிாியர்) டபிள்ᾝ. ஏ. விஸ்வா வர்ணபால) (The Hon. (Prof.) W.A. Wiswa Warnapala) එෙහම නම් - නිෙයෝජɕ කථානායකතුමා (பிரதிச் சபாநாயகர் அவர்கள்) (The Deputy Speaker) සභාගත කරන්න. ගරු මහාචාර්ය ඩබ්ලිව්. ඒ. විශ්වා වර්ණපාල මහතා (மாண்ᾗமிகு (ேபராசிாியர்) டபிள்ᾝ. ஏ. விஸ்வா வர்ணபால) (The Hon. (Prof.) W.A. Wiswa Warnapala)

Okay. ගරු නිෙයෝජɕ කථානායකතුමනි, “Progress of Activities of the University Grants Commission, 2006 - 2009” කියන ෙම් ෙල්ඛනය මා හැන්සාඩ් වාර්තාවට ඇතුළත් කිරීම සඳහා සභාගත* කරනවා.

ගරු නිෙයෝජɕ කථානායකතුමනි, ඒ වාෙග්ම "ශී ලංකා සබරගමුව සරසවිෙය් උග ගැටලු" යන ෙත්මාව යටෙත් එම විශ්වවිදɕාලෙය් සිසුන් විසින් කරනු ලබන උද්ෙඝෝෂණයක් සම්බන්ධෙයන් එහි උපකුලපතිතුමා විසින් විශ්වවිදɕාල පතිපාදන ෙකොමිෂන් සභාෙව් සභාපති ෙවත එවා තිෙබන ලිපියක් මා හැන්සාඩ් වාර්තාවට ඇතුළත් කිරීම සඳහා සභාගත* කරනවා.

අපි ශී ලංකා සබරගමුව විශ්වවිදɕාලෙය් යටිතල පහසුකම් නැංවීම සඳහා ෙගන ඇති පියවරයන් එහි සඳහන් ෙවනවා.

ගරු නිෙයෝජɕ කථානායකතුමනි, අවසාන වශෙයන් මා ඔබතුමාෙග් අවසරය ඇතිව ෙම් කරුණත් සඳහන් කරන්න කැමැතියි. In our universities, ragging has been used as a

mobilization instrument. It has been used by a certain political party, by certain activists among the student group in order to convert it into an instrument of political mobilization. This is the thing which needs to be dealt with and I am planning to take measures to deal with it.

Thank you, Mr. Deputy Speaker. සභා ෙම්සය මත තබන ලද ලියවිලි : சபாபீடத்தில் ைவக்கப்பட்ட ஆவணங்கள் : Documents tabled :

Progress of Activities of the University Grants Commission

2006 - 2009 1. Progress in University Admission to Undergraduate Courses Out of a total of 201,686 students sat the G.C.E. (A.L.)

Examination held in 2006, a total of 119,955 candidates were eligible to apply for university admission for the Academic Year 2006/2007. Of them, 36.465 sought admission to universities and 17,248 were offered admission to Higher Educational Institutions. In 2007, a total of 198,183 students sat the G.C.E. (A/L)

Examination and total of 121,421 candidates were eligible to apply for university admission for the academic year 2007.2008. Of them, 28/603 had applied for admission to universities and 20,069 were offered admission to Higher Educational Institutions. A total of 207,436 students sat the G.C.E. (A/L) Examination in

2008 and 130,236 students and fulfilled the minimum requirements for university admission of which, 46,010 had applied for the academic year 2008/2009. Of them 20,846 students were offered admission to Higher Educational Institutions in 2009. 2008/2009 NEW DEGREE COURSES (06) 1. MANAGEMENT & INFORMATION TECHNOLOGY 2. ANIMAL SCIENCE & FISHERIES 3. FOOD PRODUCTION & TECHNOLOGY MANAGEMENT 4. AQUATIC RESOURCES TECHNOLOGY 5. PALM AND LATEX TECHNOLOGY & VALUE ADDITION 6. HOSPITALITY, TOURISM EVENTS MANAGEMENT 2. Synchronization of Academic Calendar of Universities The UGC having had several programmes in the last few years to synchronize academic activities in universities managed in June 2008 to fix common days for the commencement and the end of the undergraduate academic programmes of all universities with effect from the academic year 2008/2009. Accordingly, new entrants would be admitted to Universities/HEIs in the last week of May each year and the Faculties have been permitted to decide the academic year plan based on semesters/terms. UGC has already issued a Circular in this regard, which came into effect from 1st September 2008. Unfortunately due to the delay in releasing the rescrutinized marks, the UGC was compelled to delay admission until August this year, but action has already been taken to ensure that the scheduled dates of the common calendar will be met next year onwards. 3. Academic Development (1) Expansion of University Education The UGC granted approval for establishment of the following new Standing Committees, Faculties and Departments in order to expand the university education to suit the current needs and market demands in higher education. (a) Establishment of New Standing Committees In addition to the 13 Standing Committees functioning in the University Grants Commission, which have been set up for assisting and advising the Commission on matters relevant to various disciplines such as Medicine, Agriculture, Sciences, Management Studies, Humanities and Social Sciences and other areas such as Postgraduate Studies, Information Technology, Quality Assurance, Teaching of English, Staff Development etc., 3 new Standing Committees were set up during the last 3 years. Standing Committee on Indigenous Medicine—2007 Standing Committee on Education and Distance Education - 2008/2009 Interim Board for External Degree Programmes - 2008/2009 (b) Establishment of New Faculties 1. Faculty of Medical & Allied Sciences, Rajarata University of Sri Lanka with the following Departments; * Department of anatomy * Department of Physiology * Department of Bio-Chemistry (c) Establishment of New Departments 36 new Departments were established during the last 3 years (10) in 2008/2009, 16 in 2007/2008 and 10 in 2006/2007) in the university system as follows;

(2) Reviewing external degree programmes External Degree Programmes are offered by 11 Universities/HEIs at present. There were concerns expressed at various for a regarding the quality of these degrees and the external graduates, recently. Therefore a workshop was held in September 2008 to discuss the status and idenitify solutions for the existing problems and constraints faced by External Degree Programmes. As a follow up action, on the recommendation by the said workshop, action has been initiated to establish a Board for External Degrees and the proposed Board will take action to review the external Degree programmes in future. (3) Regularization of Postgraduate Programmes (a) With a view to regularize the postgraduate programmes conducted by Universities & HEIs the Commission appointed a committee to study the issues including generating income through postgraduate courses and other extension services by Higher Educational Institutions and make recommendations. As an outcome of the study, it was decided that all Postgraduate Programmes including those conducted by Postgraduate Institutes must be channeled through the Faculty of Graduate Studies of the University. The Commission also instructed all the Universities and HEIs to obtain prior approval of the UGC for conducting such postgraduate courses. UGC initiated action accordingly to identify the necessary changes in the Act/Ordinances to implement the above changes. (b) The Commission granted approval accordingly to commence the following Postgraduate Degree/Diploma Programmes during the last year having considered the proposals made by the Universities/HEIs; * MSc in Animal Science, Faculty of Agriculture, University of Ruhuna * MSc in Nanoscience & Nanotechnology, Postgraduate Institute of Science, University of Peradeniya * MA in Regional Development and Planning, Faculty of Graduate Studies, University of Colombo * MSc/PG Diploma in Material Science Programme, Faculty of Engineering, University of Moratuwa * M.Sc. In Biodiversity, Ecotourism and Environment Management-Postgraduate Institute of Science, University of Peradeniya * Master of Science in Agri Business Mangement/Postgraduate Diploma in Agri Busincess Management- Faculty of Agriculture, University of Ruhuna * Postgraduate Diploma in Information Systems Management and Master of Information Systems Management - Faculty of Graduate Studies, University of Colombo * M.A. in Political Science in Democracy. Conflict and Governance studies (MA - DECAES) Faculty of Arts, University of Colombo * MBA in E-Governmance/PG Dip in Business Administration Specilized in E-Governance - Department of Computer Science and Engineering, University of Moratuwa * Ph. D Degree Programme in Library Information Science at National Institute of Library and Information Science, (NILIS) * Master’s Degree Programme in Social Work at the National Institute of Social Development (NISD)

(4) Common Credit and Qualification Framework for all Universities The University Grants Commission having noted that there is a significant variation in the degree awarding criteria as well as in the structure of degree programmes conducted by different faculties/universities within the Sri Lankan University System decided to formulate a common Credit and Qualification Framework for Sri Lankan University System in order to maintain the consistency and comparability of university level qualifications. As such, a Commission Circular on “Common grades, grade point value for courses and cutoff levels of GPA for awarding classes/passes” was issued by the UGC on 25.11.2008. (5) Appointment of Subject Committees The Standing Committee on Quality Assurance and Accreditation having realized the importance of contribution that the Inter-Universithy Subject Committees can make toward the enhancement of quality assurance activities in the university sector recommenced to appoint Subject Committees. The Commission accordingly approved the appointment of 40 Subject Committees comprising of 602 members and Subject benchmarking is expected to be initiated during 2009. 4. Fund Allocation Funds allocated to the University System during the last 3 years under recurrent and capital grants are as follows; Government Grants for HEIs 2007 2008 2009 Recurrent (Rs. in Millions) 9,974 10,940 11,176 Capital (Rs. in Millions Construction of Buildings 3,026 2,883 3,337 Rehabilitation & Improvement 584 744 414 of Assets Acquisition of Fixed Assets 984 1,116 699 IT Development 150 186 85 Total Capital (Rs. in Millions) 4,744 4,929 4,535 Release of Funds by the Treasury as a % of Grant 2007 2008 2009 (up to June) Recurrent 93.62% 90.50% 45% Capital 64.75% 58.50% 25% 5. Progress of Human Resources (a) Increase in the Cadre Despite the financial constraints faced by the General Treasury, the Management Services Department was kind enough to grant approval to increase the cadre in the University System during the last three years. As shown below the total Cadre of the University System was increased from 18006 in 2005/2006 to 19705 in 2008/2009, Compared to the previous year a total of 1412 new Cadre positions were created last year of which 734 are for academic positions. (b) Award of Scholarships, Fellowships and Research grants to University Academics In keeping with the UGC policy to facilitate and encourage the academic staff specially the young academics to pursue their higher studies locally and abroad and also to foster and strengthen the research culture in the university system, the UGC made concerted effort during the last 3 years to allocate more funds. In order to achieve the said objective, following grants were made available from various sources; (i) Local Research Grants for Ph.d. Research Degrees The University Grants Commission made arrangements to grant Rs. 10,105,000/- for 45 academic staff members in 2007 and Rs. 5,450,000/- for 26 academic staff members of the University System in 2008 to enhance the opportunities to obtain postgraduate qualifications under Local Research Grants for Ph.D. Research Degrees. Rs. 25,000,000/- has been allocated for 50 grantees under this Scheme during the year 2009. (ii) M. Phil/Ph.D. Placements in Indian Universities for Probationary/Senior Lecturers in Humanities, Social Sciences and Management Arrangements were made to provide financial assistance to 10 candidates to read for MA/M.Phil/Ph.D in Indian Universities in 2007 while a grant of Rs. 300,000/- each to 04 candidates were given during the year 2008 to read for Postgraduate Degrees Leading to MA/M.Phil / Ph.D. in Indian Universities.

(iii) Award of Commonwealth Scholarships and Fellowships 2006/2007 2007/2008 2008/2009 Commonwealth 15 14 14 Split Site Commonwealth 20 20 20 Fellowships 6. Infrastructure Development Infrastructure development is an area which has been given special attention by the Commission during the last 3 years. 35 construction projects have been completed in the university system during this period in order to provide facilities for teaching / learning, hostel accommodation for students, libraries etc. Total cost estimate of these 35 projects amounts to Rs.4514 mn. There are 49 on-going projects of which the total cost estimate amounts to Rs.10,429 mn commenced during the last 3 years and work-in-progress at present in the university system and 12 of them have been commenced in 2006, 10 in 2007 and 23 in 2008. In addition, there are 31 construction projects amounts to Rs.6,678 mn for which approval of the national planning has been obtained and 18 projects of which the total estimated cost is Rs.4,020 mn approved by the Cabinet of Ministers awaiting commencement of construction. The total value of the 32 projects to be commenced in 2009/2010 amounts to Rs.5,438 mn. The Commission as a policy has decided to give priority in future to improve the infrastructure facilities in the universities located in the Northern and the Eastern Provinces and also the newly established universities located in the remote areas, which do not have adequate facilities for teaching / learning environment.

Expansion of Library Facilities In order to expand the library facilities in the universities,

additional funds were granted to six selected Universities to purchase Library Automation Software Packages during the last year and new buildings have been provided on a priority basis taking into consideration the needs. In order to assure the quality of libraries in the University System a

series of workshops were held with the assistance of the Quality Assurance and Accreditation Council and a handbook was published giving the guidelines as to how the services could be improved. Libraries are now in the process of evaluating the quality. “Inter Library Loan Code”, a policy documents on issuing

materials to other libraries and borrowing materials from other libraries on loan basis for the use of readers, was prepared and finalized and this code will be used by university libraries widening the access for information to readers. A policy document on “Minimum Standards for University

Libraries” was approved by the Standing Committee in order to upgrade the service standards of university libraries in Sri Lanka. 8. Project Monitoring Project monitoring unit was established in the UGC a. to evaluate new infrastructure development projects b. to monitor the progress of on going capital projects As a policy, priority is given for newly established universities and

universities in the North and the East in the infrastructure development. Under this scheme reports were regularly obtained and on-spot

visits are made by the officials of the UGC to ensure the progress of the projects. 9. Introduction of a Centralized Information System for

Strengthening and Supporting Activities of UGC and Universities The National Higher Education Information System (N HEMIS) is

developed to provide information for planning, monitoring and evaluation for the entire higher education sector, with World Bank funds. This IT based intranet facility will enhance quality and efficiency of the management within the system. The proposed Centralized Information System (CIS) will meet the requirements of the UGC, universities, undergraduates, graduates & other stakeholders. This system will also be a tool for management / monitoring of activities in the Universities and the UGC, in the areas of university admission, student placement & tracking human resource administration etc.

පාර්ලිෙම්න්තුව 1879 1880

10. Strengthening Inter University Gommunication & Development Voice Over Internet Protocol (VOIP) and Video Conferencing provide sophisticated and cost effective media for interuniversity communication. All universities are connected via Lanka Education And Research Network [LEARN] and recently the backbone w as upgraded through Improve Relevance and Quality of University Education [IRQUEL], a World Bank funded project. Communication over telephone among universities can be done free of charge by using the VOIP facility. Video conferencing, which has already been installed will reduce the communication gap further. 11. An IT Policy for Higher Education Sector The Government has invested extensively in information technology education in Universities and promoting the use of IT in assisting administration, monitoring and other functions of the System. In order to ensure the proper usage of the computer system by all staff and authorized users in an effective, ethical and lawful manner the UGC has implemented a “User IT policy” for the Secretariat. The Commission decided to encourage Universities and HEls too to set up parameters for using IT resources in education, learning and administration and to have a code of practice for users. The UGC initiated the activity through the IT Standing Committee, subsequently, a workshop was organized for representatives for University/HEls. 12. Department of data base on national research and development A Memorandum of Understanding was signed between the National Science Foundation and the University Grants Commission on 25.01.2008 to collect information and prepare a date base on national research and development. Accordingly a survey was carried out by the UGC for the year 2006/ 2007 and a data base has been developed by using collected information. The date base is being updated annually. 13. Student Related Matters Special attention has been paid by the University Grants Commission to minimize student protests and to strengthen relationships between the university administration and students. Following precautionary measures were taken during the last two years accordingly by the University Grants Commission to minimize / avoid student problems and for the wellbeing of students in Universities and Higher Educational Institutes. (a) Protecting students from unruly elements The University Grants Commission, in order to safeguard the students from unruly elements, instructed all Vice Chancellors of Universities. Directors of Institutes and Rectors of Campuses to address all parents through a letter requesting them to protect their children from unruly political elements in universities and be vigilant of their childrens’ behavior. (b) Avoiding student unrest The University Grants Commission noted that in general due attention is not paid to student problems in universities and that is the main cause for student unrest. Therefore the Commission requested all university authorities to meet student representatives at least once a month and address their issues wherever possible in order to avoid student unrest. (c) Measures to eliminate false information among people Although the universities are doing a lot for the wellbeing of students, no adequate publicity is given on such activities, Accordingly, the Universities/Higher Educational Institutes

and Campuses were requested to give adequate publicity with regard to the actions taken by them for the wellbeing of students in order to make the public aware of such activities and to eliminate false information among people about the facilities provided to students for them to pursuer their higher studies. (d) Minimizing ragging incidents A document prepared by University Grants Commission on “Legal framework on ragging and establishing Student Unions in universities in Sri Lanka” was distributed among all Universities / Higher Educational Institutes in order to make students aware of the gravity Of committing ragging and other forms of violence in Universities/Campuses/Institutes and remedies available for same. (e) Recovery of cost of damages for university properties The University Grants Commission after going through the reports sent by the Universities on different student related incients noted that students have caused damages to university properties at certain instances and thus decided to make them accountable for such damages and charge the cost of damages from responsible individuals or reduce the cost of damages from the allocations made to student councils. Accordingly a Commission Circular was issued in order to safeguard student welfare. (f) Preparation of Student Charter by each University/HEI Having noticed the increased trend of student misbehavior/misconduct in universities/HEIs, action is being taken to prepare a Student Charter/Student Hand Book by each University/HEI to avoid unnecessary incidents and make students aware of the consequences of such incidents and the importance of university education. (g) Enhance Welfare Facilities for Students The University Grants Commission is in the process of collecting information on availability of safe drinking water, hygienic sanitation facilities and waste disposal mechanisms from all Universities and HEIs in order to improve the same with the intention of improving better learning environment for students. (h) Student Support Service Units

Actions are being taken to establish Student Support Service Units in Universities in order to upgrade standards with emphasis on teaching/learning and allied services and facilities. (i) Training opportunities for university students in Public and Private Sector Having recognized the importance of providing training opportunities for their students in public/private sector organizations the universities have been requested to include a training/internship component in the curriculum wherever possible and most of the universities have already taken action to provide training opportunities for their students accordingly. 14. financial Assistance to University Students There are 03 main schemes under which university students are assisted financially, They are; 1. Mahapola Scholarship Scheme 2. University Bursary Scheme 3. Endowed Scholarship Scheme (Out of funds donated by various individuals, institutions and associations)

Uthuru Wasaanthaya His Excellency the President has launched “Vadakkin Wasantham - Uthuru Wasanthaya - Awakening North” programme to entail the welfare and rehabilitation of all citizens including all youths, children and women of the war-torn Northern Province. Under this programme the Vauniya campus has been allocated Rs.35 Million to improve the learning environment, library services, hostel facilities and improve mobility of students. Rs 15 Million is allocated to the University of Jaffna for activities such as improvement of student welfare, hostel accommodation and improvement/upgrading sanitation facilities. The above activities will be funded by the World Bank through the IRQUE project and it is to be completed in 6 months. A Steering Committee has been appointed to monitor and supervise the above activities and the Committee is responsible for implementation of the Proposal in line with the Government action plan. 16. Univeristy Industry Community Interaction Cells (UICIC) On the instructions of the University Grants Commission/Universities have taken steps to set up University Industry Community Interaction Cells (UICIC), in the form of Technology Incubators, Science Parks and Business Cells in Universities and HEIs, to serve as centers for imparting knowledge and technology to industry, community and to the general public in their needs. Under this programme, which has been included in the “Mahinda Chinthana” programme too, areas in the vicinity of universities are expected to be developed as ‘university villages’ Some universities have already started collaborative peogrammes with villages in order to address their problems in the areas of agriculture, industry, education etc. 17. Appointment of Committees to make recommendations to improve the functional capacity of Universities / HEIs Two Committees were appointed by the UGC to examine the quality of academic and general administration and to make recommendations to improve the functional capacity of Wayamba University Sri Lanka, Institute of Indigenous Medicine and Gampaha Wickramarachchi Ayurveda Institute. Both Committees were chaired by Members of the Commission and submitted their recommendations after having investigated into the academic & administrative issues of those HEIs for long lasting solutions and the respective HEIs have been requested to implement some of those recommendations while the UGC is attending to others. 18. Recognition of Degrees The Department of Inter University Affairs of the UGC handles a large number of requests for recognition of Degrees, Diplomas, Certificates and other Academic Distinctions obtained by Sri

Lankan students form foreign Universities and Higher Educational Institutions every year. Certain arrangements have been made for streamlining the process of issuing such recognition certificate due to complexity of issues faced by the UGC. To regularize the Processing of applications for recognition of Qualifications/Degree Awarding Institutions, a Committee consisting of four Commission members was appointed accordingly by the UGC. The Committee makes recommendations on requests for Recognition of Qualifications/Degree Awarding Institutions to the UGC. A format has also been developed for application for Degree Awarding Status by Institutions and also for Recognition of Professional qualifications for eligibility to enter postgraduate course in Sri Lankan universities. Adequate publicity was given to the general public through mass media warning the prospective candidates to verify the authenticity and recognition of foreign Universities/Higher Educational Institutions at which they wish to get enrolled for their higher studies prior to leaving the country or such enrolment. 19. Recognition of Degree Awarding Institutes Under Section 25A of the Universities Act No. 16 of 1978, the Minister may recognize, any Institution as a Degree Awarding Institute for the purpose of developing higher Education. As the Specified Authority designated for the purpose, the UGC has taken measures to recognize the following degrees offered by the following Institutes during the period under review. National Institute of Social Development Master of Social Works Degree (MSW) Sri Lanka Institute for Development Administration (SLIDA) MBA (General) MBA (Finance) MBA (Human Resources Management) MBA (Project Management) MBA (Information Technology) National Institute of Business Management (NIBM) B. Sc in Business Management [Specialized areas: Human Resource Management, Logistics, Project Management and Industrial Management] B.Sc in Management Information Systems 20. Improving Financial Management Considering the observations made by the Auditor general and the Committee on Public Enterprises [COPE] of Parliament, an Audit Action & Monitoring Committee [Mini - COPE] was set up by the UGC to regularly review the management of funds by theHEIs. This Committee meets on a regular basis with the Secretary to the line Ministry in Chair and it has helped the Universities and HEIs to identify the Lapses, weaknesses and shortcomings of internal control systems and procedures ensuring adherence to Good Governance and Management practices introduced by the Treasury in keeping with financial regulations. 21. Strengthening Internal Security of Higher Educational Institutions Due to the concerns expressed by Vice-Chancellors on deterioration of discipline in HEIs, a discussion was held with the IGP and other officials under the Chaimanship of Hon. Minister of Higher Education. Consequent to this meeting action was taken to set up police posts at EUSL, SEUSL and Trincomalee Campus as a priority measure. Furthermore as agreed upon at the discussions held with the IGP, all HEIs have been requested to regularly liaise with Senior Police Officers in the area in order to maintain law and order in the universities.

පාර්ලිෙම්න්තුව 1883 1884

22. Progress Meetings with the Hon. Minister of Higher Education The Hon. Minister of Higher Education has decided to conduct a series of meetings with the University Community including academics, administrators and others in order to streamline the University Education System amd to monitor the progress of activities. Several such meetings were already held in the UGC and the most recently following groups were met. (a) Meeting with the Directors of all Postgraduate Institutes. The purpose of the meeting was to discuss the issues pertaining to postgraduate education in the university system in order to create a vibrant intellectual culture in the country. (b) Meeting with the Registrars and Bursars of Universities The purpose of the meeting was to discuss the role of the Registrar and the Bursar in driving the universities to make them global centers of excellence. 23. Contribution to the establishment of the South Asian University in New Delhi, India Establishment of the South Asian University as a centre of excellence by pooling the rrsources available within the SAARC member states is in progress. The University will be set up in close proximity to New Delhi, India. The Chairman and the Vice-Chairman of the UGC serve as members of the Steering Committee which has been set up for planning and establishment of the South Asian University. Prof Sarath Abayakoon, former member of the Commission and present Vice Chancellor of the University of Peradeniya has been appointed as a Consultant/Advisor on Infrastructure Development.
